proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-backquote-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(setq nelisp-backquote-proof-x '(b c))
(setq nelisp-backquote-proof-y '(d e))
(let* ((simple (eval (cdr (backquote-process
                           (list 'a (list backquote-unquote-symbol 'nelisp-backquote-proof-x) 'z)))))
       (spliced (eval (cdr (backquote-process
                            (list 'a (list backquote-splice-symbol 'nelisp-backquote-proof-y) 'z)))))
       (vector-result (eval (cdr (backquote-process
                                  (vector 'v (list backquote-unquote-symbol 'nelisp-backquote-proof-x)))))))
  (and (featurep 'backquote)
       (fboundp 'backquote-process)
       (fboundp 'backquote-delay-process)
       (fboundp 'backquote-listify)
       (fboundp 'backquote-list*)
       (macrop 'backquote)
       (macrop 'backquote-list*-macro)
       (equal (backquote-list*-function 'a 'b '(c d)) '(a b c d))
       (equal (backquote-list* 'a 'b '(c d)) '(a b c d))
       (equal simple '(a (b c) z))
       (equal spliced '(a d e z))
       (equal vector-result [v (b c)])))
EOF
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast \
  VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=180s \
  VENDOR_REPL_INTERNAL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=150 \
  VENDOR_FAST_FILES="$(pwd)/vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/backquote.el" \
  VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM_FILE="$proof"
rm -f "$proof"

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-timer-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(defun nelisp-timer-proof-fn (&rest args) args)
(let ((timer-list nil)
      (timer-idle-list nil)
      (timer (timer-create)))
  (timer-set-time timer (current-time) 3)
  (timer-set-function timer #'nelisp-timer-proof-fn '(alpha beta))
  (timer-activate timer)
  (and (featurep 'timer)
       (timerp timer)
       (fboundp 'timer-create)
       (fboundp 'timer-set-time)
       (fboundp 'timer-set-idle-time)
       (fboundp 'timer-set-function)
       (fboundp 'timer-activate)
       (fboundp 'timer-activate-when-idle)
       (fboundp 'cancel-timer)
       (fboundp 'cancel-function-timers)
       (fboundp 'run-at-time)
       (fboundp 'run-with-timer)
       (fboundp 'run-with-idle-timer)
       (macrop 'with-timeout)
       (eq (timer--function timer) #'nelisp-timer-proof-fn)
       (equal (timer--args timer) '(alpha beta))
       (= (timer--repeat-delay timer) 3)
       (memq timer timer-list)
       (progn (cancel-timer timer) t)
       (not (memq timer timer-list))
       (let ((idle (timer-create)))
         (timer-set-idle-time idle 5 t)
         (timer-set-function idle #'nelisp-timer-proof-fn '(idle))
         (timer-activate-when-idle idle)
         (and (memq idle timer-idle-list)
              (eq (timer--idle-delay idle) 'idle)
              (eq (timer--repeat-delay idle) t)
              (progn (cancel-timer idle) t)
              (not (memq idle timer-idle-list))))))
EOF
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast \

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-float-sup-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(let ((pi-delta (abs (- float-pi (* 4 (atan 1)))))
      (e-delta (abs (- float-e (exp 1))))
      (rad (degrees-to-radians 180.0))
      (deg (radians-to-degrees float-pi)))
  (and (featurep 'lisp-float-type)
       (boundp 'float-pi)
       (boundp 'float-e)
       (boundp 'degrees-to-radians)
       (boundp 'radians-to-degrees)
       (macrop 'degrees-to-radians)
       (macrop 'radians-to-degrees)
       (boundp 'pi)
       (equal (get 'pi 'byte-obsolete-variable) '(float-pi nil "23.3"))
       (< pi-delta 0.0000000001)
       (< e-delta 0.0000000001)
       (< (abs (- rad float-pi)) 0.0000000001)
       (< (abs (- deg 180.0)) 0.0000000001)))
EOF
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast \

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-float-sup-coalesce-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(let ((deg-expanded (macroexpand '(degrees-to-radians 180.0)))
      (rad-expanded (macroexpand '(radians-to-degrees float-pi))))
  (and (featurep 'lisp-float-type)
       (boundp 'float-pi)
       (boundp 'float-e)
       (boundp 'degrees-to-radians)
       (boundp 'radians-to-degrees)
       (boundp 'pi)
       (macrop 'degrees-to-radians)
       (macrop 'radians-to-degrees)
       (floatp float-pi)
       (floatp float-e)
       (> float-pi 3.14)
       (< float-pi 3.15)
       (> float-e 2.71)
       (< float-e 2.72)
       (equal deg-expanded (list '* degrees-to-radians 180.0))
       (equal rad-expanded (list '* radians-to-degrees 'float-pi))))
EOF

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-tq-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(defvar nelisp-tq-proof-result nil)
(defun nelisp-tq-proof-callback (closure answer)
  (setq nelisp-tq-proof-result (list closure answer)))
(let* ((buf (generate-new-buffer " *nelisp-tq-proof*"))
       (tq (cons nil (cons nil buf))))
  (unwind-protect
      (progn
        (tq-queue-add tq "question" "END" 'closure #'nelisp-tq-proof-callback)
        (tq-filter tq "payload END")
        (and (featurep 'tq)
             (fboundp 'tq-create)
             (fboundp 'tq-queue-add)
             (fboundp 'tq-queue-pop)
             (fboundp 'tq-enqueue)
             (fboundp 'tq-filter)
             (fboundp 'tq-process-buffer)
             (fboundp 'tq-close)
             (tq-queue-empty tq)
             (equal nelisp-tq-proof-result '(closure "payload END"))
             (with-current-buffer buf (= (buffer-size) 0))))
    (when (buffer-live-p buf) (kill-buffer buf))))
EOF
make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast \
  VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=180s \
  VENDOR_REPL_INTERNAL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=150 \
  VENDOR_FAST_FILES="$(pwd)/vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/tq.el" \
  VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM_FILE="$proof"
rm -f "$proof"

(let ((safe-functions nil))
  (and (featurep 'unsafep)
       (fboundp 'unsafep)
       (fboundp 'unsafep-function)
       (fboundp 'unsafep-progn)
       (fboundp 'unsafep-let)

       (null (unsafep '(+ 1 2)))
       (null (unsafep '(let ((x 1)) (+ x 2))))
       (null (unsafep '(mapcar (lambda (x) (+ x 1)) '(1 2))))
       (equal (unsafep '(delete-file "x")) '(function delete-file))
       (equal (unsafep '(setq global-value 1)) '(global-value))
       (let ((safe-functions t)) (null (unsafep '(delete-file "x"))))))
EOF

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-bindat-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(let* ((spec '((kind u8)
               (port u16)
               (name strz 6)
               (addr vec 4)))
       (struct '((kind . 7)
                 (port . 4660)
                 (name . "abc")
                 (addr . [192 168 1 9])))
       (raw (bindat-pack spec struct))
       (decoded (bindat-unpack spec raw)))
  (and (featurep 'bindat)
       (fboundp 'bindat-pack)
       (fboundp 'bindat-unpack)
       (fboundp 'bindat-length)
       (fboundp 'bindat-get-field)
       (fboundp 'bindat-vector-to-dec)
       (fboundp 'bindat-vector-to-hex)
       (fboundp 'bindat-ip-to-string)
       (stringp raw)
       (= (length raw) (bindat-length spec struct))
       (= (bindat-get-field decoded 'kind) 7)
       (= (bindat-get-field decoded 'port) 4660)
       (equal (bindat-get-field decoded 'name) "abc")
       (equal (bindat-get-field decoded 'addr) [192 168 1 9])
       (equal (bindat-vector-to-dec [192 168 1 9]) "192.168.1.9")
       (equal (bindat-vector-to-hex [10 11 12]) "0a:0b:0c")
       (equal (bindat-ip-to-string [127 0 0 1]) "127.0.0.1")))
EOF

(let ((plist (list :a 1 :b 2)))
  (and (featurep 'cl-extra)
       (featurep 'cl-lib)
       (featurep 'seq)
       (fboundp 'cl-coerce)
       (fboundp 'cl-equalp)
       (fboundp 'cl-gcd)
       (fboundp 'cl-lcm)
       (fboundp 'cl-isqrt)
       (fboundp 'cl-parse-integer)
       (fboundp 'cl-subseq)

       (equal (cl-coerce [1 2 3] 'list) '(1 2 3))
       (equal (cl-coerce '(?a ?b) 'string) "ab")
       (cl-equalp "NeLisp" "nelisp")
       (cl-equalp [1 "A"] [1.0 "a"])
       (= (cl-gcd 24 36 60) 12)
       (= (cl-lcm 6 8 9) 72)
       (= (cl-isqrt 99) 9)
       (equal (cl-floor 17 5) '(3 2))
       (equal (cl-ceiling 17 5) '(4 -3))
       (equal (cl-truncate -17 5) '(-3 -2))
       (equal (cl-round 13 5) '(3 -2))
       (= (cl-mod -17 5) 3)
       (= (cl-rem -17 5) -2)
       (= (cl-signum -22) -1)
       (= (cl-parse-integer "  -2a" :radix 16) -42)
       (equal (cl-subseq [a b c d] 1 3) [b c])
       (equal (cl-concatenate 'string "ne" "lisp") "nelisp")
       (equal (cl-revappend '(a b) '(c)) '(b a c))
       (cl-tailp (cdr plist) plist)
       (= (cl-getf plist :b) 2)
       (equal (cl-getf plist :missing 'fallback) 'fallback)))
EOF

cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(let* ((fv1 (cconv-fv '(+ x y) '(x) '(y)))
       (fv2 (cconv-fv '#'(lambda (z) (+ x z dyn)) '(x) '(dyn))))
  (and (featurep 'cconv)
       (fboundp 'cconv-closure-convert)
       (fboundp 'cconv-convert)
       (fboundp 'cconv-fv)
       (fboundp 'cconv-make-interpreted-closure)
       (equal (cconv--set-diff '(a b c) '(b)) '(a c))
       (equal (cconv--set-diff-map '(a b c) '((b . 2))) '(a c))
       (equal (cconv--map-diff '((a . 1) (b . 2) (c . 3)) '((b . 9))) '((a . 1) (c . 3)))
       (equal (cconv--map-diff-elem '((a . 1) (b . 2)) 'a) '((b . 2)))
       (equal (cconv--map-diff-set '((a . 1) (b . 2) (c . 3)) '(a c)) '((b . 2)))
       (member 'x (car fv1))
       (member 'y (cdr fv1))
       (member 'x (car fv2))
       (member 'dyn (cdr fv2))))
EOF

(let ((icon-preference '(text symbol emoji image)))

    :help-echo "parent help")

    "Child proof icon."
    :version "30.1"
    :help-echo "child help")
  (let* ((spec (icon-complete-spec 'nelisp-proof-child))
         (text-spec (assq 'text spec))
         (s (icon-string 'nelisp-proof-child))

         (featurep 'cl-lib)

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-hierarchy-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(let* ((parents '((a . root) (b . root) (c . b)))
       (h (hierarchy-new))
       copy extracted mapped rendered)
  (hierarchy-add-trees h '(root a b c)
                       (lambda (item) (cdr (assq item parents))))
  (hierarchy-sort h (lambda (x y) (string< (symbol-name x) (symbol-name y))))
  (setq copy (hierarchy-copy h))
  (setq extracted (hierarchy-extract-tree h 'b))
  (setq mapped (hierarchy-map (lambda (item indent) (list item indent)) h))
  (setq rendered (hierarchy-to-string h (lambda (item) (symbol-name item))))
  (and (featurep 'hierarchy)
       (featurep 'seq)
       (featurep 'map)
       (featurep 'subr-x)
       (featurep 'cl-lib)
       (hierarchy-p h)
       (= (hierarchy-length h) 4)
       (equal (hierarchy-roots h) '(root))
       (equal (hierarchy-children h 'root) '(a b))
       (equal (hierarchy-children h 'b) '(c))
       (equal (sort (copy-sequence (hierarchy-leafs h))
                    (lambda (x y) (string< (symbol-name x) (symbol-name y))))
              '(a c))
       (eq (hierarchy-parent h 'c) 'b)
       (hierarchy-descendant-p h 'c 'root)
       (not (hierarchy-descendant-p h 'root 'c))
       (hierarchy-equal h copy)
       (hierarchy-has-item extracted 'root)
       (hierarchy-has-item extracted 'b)
       (hierarchy-has-item extracted 'c)
       (not (hierarchy-has-item extracted 'a))
       (equal mapped '((root 0) (a 1) (b 1) (c 2)))
       (string-match-p "root" rendered)
       (string-match-p "  c" rendered)))
EOF

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-elp-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(defun nelisp-elp-proof-target (x) (+ x 10))
(let ((elp-function-list nil)
      (elp-record-p t)
      (elp-master nil)
      info result ok)
  (unwind-protect
      (progn
        (setq ok
              (and (featurep 'elp)
                   (fboundp 'elp-instrument-function)
                   (fboundp 'elp-restore-function)
                   (fboundp 'elp-reset-function)
                   (fboundp 'elp-set-master)
                   (fboundp 'elp-unset-master)
                   (fboundp 'elp-profilable-p)
                   (fboundp 'elp--instrumented-p)
                   (elp-profilable-p 'nelisp-elp-proof-target)))
        (elp-instrument-function 'nelisp-elp-proof-target)
        (setq result (nelisp-elp-proof-target 5))
        (setq info (get 'nelisp-elp-proof-target elp-timer-info-property))
        (setq ok (and ok
                      (= result 15)
                      (elp--instrumented-p 'nelisp-elp-proof-target)
                      (vectorp info)
                      (= (aref info 0) 1)
                      (numberp (aref info 1))))
        (elp-reset-function 'nelisp-elp-proof-target)
        (setq ok (and ok
                      (= (aref info 0) 0)
                      (= (aref info 1) 0.0)))
        (elp-set-master 'nelisp-elp-proof-target)
        (setq ok (and ok (eq elp-master 'nelisp-elp-proof-target) (not elp-record-p)))
        (elp-unset-master)
        (setq ok (and ok (null elp-master) elp-record-p))
        (elp-restore-function 'nelisp-elp-proof-target)
        (and ok
             (not (elp--instrumented-p 'nelisp-elp-proof-target))
             (null (get 'nelisp-elp-proof-target elp-timer-info-property))
             (= (nelisp-elp-proof-target 2) 12)))
    (when (fboundp 'nelisp-elp-proof-target)
      (ignore-errors (elp-restore-function 'nelisp-elp-proof-target)))))
EOF

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-trace-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(defun nelisp-trace-proof-target (x y) (+ x y))
(let ((trace-buffer "*nelisp-trace-proof*")
      (ok nil)
      result text)
  (unwind-protect
      (progn
        (setq ok
              (and (featurep 'trace)
                   (featurep 'cl-print)
                   (commandp 'trace-function)
                   (commandp 'trace-function-foreground)
                   (commandp 'trace-function-background)
                   (commandp 'untrace-function)
                   (commandp 'untrace-all)
                   (fboundp 'trace-make-advice)
                   (fboundp 'trace-function-internal)
                   (fboundp 'trace-is-traced)
                   (fboundp 'trace-values)))
        (trace-function-background 'nelisp-trace-proof-target trace-buffer)
        (setq ok (and ok (trace-is-traced 'nelisp-trace-proof-target)))
        (setq result (nelisp-trace-proof-target 4 5))
        (setq text (with-current-buffer trace-buffer (buffer-string)))
        (untrace-function 'nelisp-trace-proof-target)
        (and ok
             (= result 9)
             (not (trace-is-traced 'nelisp-trace-proof-target))
             (string-match-p "nelisp-trace-proof-target" text)
             (string-match-p "4" text)
             (string-match-p "5" text)
             (string-match-p "9" text)
             (= (nelisp-trace-proof-target 1 2) 3)))
    (ignore-errors (untrace-function 'nelisp-trace-proof-target))
    (when (get-buffer trace-buffer)
      (kill-buffer trace-buffer))))
EOF

proof="$(mktemp /tmp/nelisp-shadow-proof.XXXXXX.el)"
cat > "$proof" <<'EOF'
(let* ((base (make-temp-file "nelisp-shadow" t))
       (d1 (expand-file-name "one" base))
       (d2 (expand-file-name "two" base))
       (load-path-shadows-compare-text nil)
       shadows report ok)
  (make-directory d1)
  (make-directory d2)
  (write-region "(provide 'same)\n" nil (expand-file-name "same.el" d1) nil 'silent)
  (write-region "(provide 'same)\n" nil (expand-file-name "same.el" d2) nil 'silent)
  (write-region "(provide 'only-one)\n" nil (expand-file-name "only-one.el" d1) nil 'silent)
  (setq shadows (load-path-shadows-find (list d1 d2)))
  (let ((load-path (list d1 d2)))
    (setq report (list-load-path-shadows t)))
  (setq ok
        (and (featurep 'shadow)
             (fboundp 'load-path-shadows-find)
             (fboundp 'load-path-shadows-same-file-or-nonexistent)
             (commandp 'list-load-path-shadows)
             (fboundp 'load-path-shadows-mode)
             (boundp 'load-path-shadows-font-lock-keywords)
             (= (length shadows) 2)
             (string-match-p "/same$" (car shadows))
             (string-match-p "/same$" (cadr shadows))
             (string-match-p "same hides" report)
             (string-match-p "1 Emacs Lisp load-path shadowing was found" report)))
  (delete-directory base t)
  ok)
EOF

(let* ((normal-a (list nil [" " "       2.0" "        1.0" "beta"]))
       (normal-b (list nil [" " "       3.0" "        2.0" "alpha"]))
       (idle-a (list nil ["   *" "       1.0" "        1.0" "idle"]))
       ok)
  (setq ok
        (and (featurep 'timer)
             (featurep 'tabulated-list)
             (featurep 'timer-list)
             (commandp 'list-timers)
             (commandp 'timer-list-cancel)
             (fboundp 'timer-list-mode)

             (fboundp 'timer-list--next-predicate)

             (fboundp 'timer-list--function-predicate)
             (keymapp timer-list-mode-map)
             (eq (lookup-key timer-list-mode-map (kbd "c")) 'timer-list-cancel)
             (timer-list--next-predicate normal-a normal-b)
             (timer-list--repeat-predicate normal-a normal-b)
             (not (timer-list--function-predicate normal-a normal-b))
             (not (timer-list--idle-predicate idle-a normal-a))
             (timer-list--idle-predicate normal-a idle-a)
             (with-temp-buffer
               (timer-list-mode)

                    (eq revert-buffer-function 'list-timers)
                    (vectorp tabulated-list-format)
                    (= (length tabulated-list-format) 4)

                    (equal (aref (aref tabulated-list-format 3) 0) "Function"))))))
  ok)
EOF

(let* ((parsed (read-kbd-macro "C-x C-f RET" t))
       (simple (read-kbd-macro "abc" t))
       (formatted (format-kbd-macro "abc" 1))
       (roundtrip (read-kbd-macro formatted t)))
  (and (featurep 'edmacro)
       (commandp 'edit-kbd-macro)
       (commandp 'edit-last-kbd-macro)
       (commandp 'edit-named-kbd-macro)
       (commandp 'read-kbd-macro)
       (fboundp 'format-kbd-macro)
       (fboundp 'edmacro-format-keys)
       (fboundp 'edmacro-parse-keys)
       (fboundp 'edmacro-fix-menu-commands)
       (keymapp edmacro-mode-map)
       (eq (lookup-key edmacro-mode-map (kbd "C-c C-c")) 'edmacro-finish-edit)
       (eq (lookup-key edmacro-mode-map (kbd "C-c C-q")) 'edmacro-insert-key)
       (eq (lookup-key edmacro-mode-map (kbd "C-c C-r")) 'edmacro-set-macro-to-region-lines)
       (vectorp parsed)
       (= (length parsed) 3)
       (eq (aref parsed 0) 24)
       (eq (aref parsed 1) 6)
       (eq (aref parsed 2) 'return)
       (vectorp simple)
       (= (length simple) 3)
       (eq (aref simple 0) ?a)
       (eq (aref simple 1) ?b)
       (eq (aref simple 2) ?c)
       (stringp formatted)
       (string-match-p "abc" formatted)
       (vectorp roundtrip)
       (= (length roundtrip) 3)
       (eq (aref roundtrip 0) ?a)
       (eq (aref roundtrip 1) ?b)
       (eq (aref roundtrip 2) ?c)))
EOF

  VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM_ELISP="(let* ((old-prefixed (and (fboundp (quote shell-prefixed-directory-name)) (symbol-function (quote shell-prefixed-directory-name)))) (old-cd (and (fboundp (quote shell-process-cd)) (symbol-function (quote shell-process-cd)))) (target (file-name-as-directory (make-temp-file \"dirtrack-proof\" t))) (changed nil) (result nil)) (unwind-protect (progn (defalias (quote shell-prefixed-directory-name) (function identity)) (defalias (quote shell-process-cd) (lambda (dir) (setq default-directory (file-name-as-directory dir)))) (setq result (with-temp-buffer (insert \"process output\\n\") (goto-char (point-max)) (setq-local default-directory (file-name-as-directory temporary-file-directory)) (setq-local dirtrack-list (list \"^DIR:\\\\(.*\\\\)$\" 1)) (setq-local dirtrack-directory-function (function file-name-as-directory)) (setq-local dirtrack-canonicalize-function (function identity)) (setq-local dirtrack-directory-change-hook (list (lambda nil (setq changed t)))) (dirtrack-mode 1) (let ((input (concat \"DIR:\" target))) (and (featurep (quote dirtrack)) (commandp (quote dirtrack-mode)) (commandp (quote dirtrack-debug-mode)) (fboundp (quote dirtrack)) (memq (quote dirtrack) comint-preoutput-filter-functions) (string= (dirtrack input) input) changed (string= default-directory target)))))) result) (if old-prefixed (fset (quote shell-prefixed-directory-name) old-prefixed) (fmakunbound (quote shell-prefixed-directory-name))) (if old-cd (fset (quote shell-process-cd) old-cd) (fmakunbound (quote shell-process-cd)))))"

Use =VENDOR_FAST_PROOF_FORM_FILE= or =VENDOR_REPL_PROOF_FORM_FILE= when an
extracted exact vendor proof contains docstrings, backquote syntax, embedded
newlines, or other text that is awkward to pass through shell and Make
quoting.  The file should contain one raw Lisp proof form.

The direct ERT covers all currently separated =files.el= and =window.el=
top-level key wiring shapes.  The standalone single-binding checks above pass,
the synthetic three-binding =window.el= proof above passes in about 48.84s,
the four-command synthetic proof passes in about 49.37s, the two-command plus
prefix-map synthetic proof passes in about 49.27s, and the multi-map synthetic
proof above passes in about 48.90s.  A combined =files.el= + =window.el=
representative proof now passes in about 150.23s.  Existing =ctl-x-map=
is narrower now: two command bindings plus lookup pass in about 132.15s,
three command bindings define-only pass with
=VENDOR_REPL_INTERNAL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=300= in about 275.99s after rebuilding
=build/nemacs-bootstrap.repl=, and four command bindings define-only now pass
in about 149.74s after the keymap tail scan optimization and another bootstrap
rebuild.  The command-loop dispatch proof above also passes in about 150.57s:
after real vendor =files.el= + =window.el= load, a synthetic interactive
command is bound into existing =ctl-x-map=, queued via
=unread-command-events=, and reached through =command-loop-1=.  The sparse
keymap mutator now avoids redundant tail scans while preserving upstream-style
sparse/full keymap behavior.  Keep representative P2 key wiring and basic
interactive dispatch resolved.  The direct =execute-extended-command= proof
above also passes in about 231.15s after the same real vendor load path, with
raw prefix arg propagation into the dispatched interactive command.  Follow-up
P2/P6 work should focus on broader command dispatch and interactive behavior.

** Regression tests

For script/load-path changes:

#+begin_src sh
emacs -Q --batch -L scripts -L test \
  -l test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el \
  --eval "(ert-run-tests-batch-and-exit 'standalone-diagnostics-test/vendor-repl-load-paths-include-external-magit-vendors)"
#+end_src

For broader smoke:

#+begin_src sh
make test-fast
#+end_src

Run heavier library gates only when package manifests, public APIs, or
package scaffolds change.

* 6. Triage rule for failures

When a vendor replay fails:

1. Do not patch the vendor file first.
2. Identify the normalized form with =VENDOR_REPL_TRACE_FORMS=t=.
3. Reproduce the form as a smaller proof after loading the same vendor
   prerequisites.
4. Classify the failure as one of:
   - reader/bootstrap missing behavior;
   - foundation primitive;
   - CL/EIEIO/generic substrate;
   - buffer/edit substrate;
   - keymap/command substrate;
   - process/file substrate;
   - display/window substrate;
   - package load/autoload substrate.
5. Fix the lowest reusable owner.
6. Add a focused regression test that proves the substrate behavior, not the
   local workaround.
7. Re-run the original vendor replay.

* 7. What not to do

- Do not implement a local Magit status UI as a substitute for upstream
  Magit.
- Do not replace Dired with a local file manager.
- Do not replace Org parser behavior with a local parser when
  =org-element.el= is present.
- Do not treat passing host Emacs load as sufficient standalone proof.
- Do not change vendored Emacs Lisp unless the local vendor policy explicitly
  allows it and the change is recorded as a vendor patch.
- Do not use Rust reduction as an acceptance criterion.

* 8. Immediate next handoff

Continue with lightweight C-core substrate before returning to the full Magit
path:

1. P1 metadata and P8 integration substrate now have focused tests and have
   been exercised by small vendor gates.
2. Keep =dired-x.el=, =register.el=, =eieio.el=, and the minimal EIEIO
   parent/child =defclass= proof as lightweight regression gates.
3. Keep =files.el= as a lightweight load gate, but remember that its top-level
   prefix key wiring is deliberately separated from this load proof; P2 still
   owns full keymap/command-surface verification.  A direct keymap regression
   now covers the separated =files.el= key shapes, and representative
   standalone single-binding proofs pass.
4. Additional lightweight Emacs-distributed replay gates now pass:
   =button.el= for button/text-property behavior, =thingatpt.el= for
   bounds/search behavior, =case-table.el= for character table behavior,
   =help-macro.el= for help macro declarations, =subr-x.el= for extended

   behavior, =sort.el= for buffer sort/edit behavior, =view.el= for
   view/window command substrate, =paragraphs.el= / =fill.el= /

   =savehist.el= / =saveplace.el= for file/history integration,
   =time-date.el= for time/date primitives,

   =autoinsert.el= for file-template alist and find-file hook surface,
   =bs.el= for slower buffer-selection surface,

   =buff-menu.el= for tabulated Buffer Menu mode/keymap surface,

5. Keep =version.el= as a P1 metadata/version substrate gate.  It succeeds
   with =VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=180s= / =VENDOR_REPL_INTERNAL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=150=
   and the representative proof currently takes about 148.73s: after real
   vendor =version.el= load, =emacs-version= is a command, =version= is the
   upstream alias, =emacs-major-version= / =emacs-minor-version= are integers,
   =(emacs-version)= returns a string, and obsolete Bazaar version aliases
   install metadata.  This is still vendor =version.el= execution, not a local
   version shim.
6. Keep =env.el= as a slower P4 process-environment substrate gate.  It
   succeeds with =VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=300s= /
   =VENDOR_REPL_INTERNAL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=260= and the representative
   =setenv= / =getenv= overlay proof currently takes about 228.55s after real
   vendor =env.el= load.  The proof confirms that =setenv= and =getenv= are
   commands, =substitute-env-vars= is defined, a local =process-environment=
   binding is read by =getenv=, existing variables can be replaced, new
   variables can be added, and unrelated entries stay visible.  The stronger
   overlay round-trip plus =substitute-env-vars= integration proof
   ("$NEMACS_T=x" -> "2=x") now passes as of 2026-07-03 with
   =VENDOR_REPL_TIMEOUT=320s= / =VENDOR_REPL_INTERNAL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=280= in
   about 74.51s, down from 228.55s at the 300/260 budget.  The earlier
   150s-budget timeout was the NeLisp standalone allocator/GC scaling boundary
   fixed on the NeLisp side (commits =0be0e1d6= / =79550f98= / =a2842b03= /
   =5a337c8f=), not missing Emacs substrate.  This is still vendor =env.el=
   execution, not a local environment shim.

   separates top-level =global-map= / =ctl-x-map= / =ctl-x-4-map= command
   wiring from load replay.  A direct keymap regression now covers those
   separated =window.el= key shapes.  Standalone single-binding proofs pass,

   (=C-x 2=, =C-x 3=, and =C-x 0= shapes on a fresh sparse map) now passes
   in about 48.84s.  A four-command synthetic proof passes in about 49.37s,
   a two-command plus prefix-map synthetic proof passes in about 49.27s, and
   a multi-map synthetic proof with two command bindings, one command binding
   on another sparse map, and one prefix-map binding passes in about 48.90s.
   Existing =ctl-x-map= is now reduced further: two command bindings plus
   lookup pass in about 132.15s, and three command bindings define-only pass
   with =VENDOR_REPL_INTERNAL_TIMEOUT_SECONDS=300= in about 275.99s after
   rebuilding =build/nemacs-bootstrap.repl=.  Four command bindings
   define-only now pass in about 149.74s after the keymap tail scan
   optimization and another bootstrap rebuild.  A combined =files.el= +
   =window.el= representative proof now passes in about 150.23s.  The sparse
   keymap mutator now avoids redundant tail scans while preserving
   upstream-style sparse/full keymap behavior.  =call-interactively= and
   =command-execute= now reject non-interactive functions with
   =wrong-type-argument commandp=, matching Emacs' command boundary.  A
   command-loop dispatch proof after real vendor =files.el= + =window.el=
   load now passes in about 150.57s: a synthetic interactive command is bound
   into existing =ctl-x-map=, queued via =unread-command-events=, and reached
   through =command-loop-1=.  Direct =execute-extended-command= dispatch to a
   synthetic interactive command with raw prefix arg now passes in about
   231.15s after the same real vendor load path.  =execute-extended-command=
   also has a focused non-command rejection regression, so
   =call-interactively=, =command-execute=, and =execute-extended-command=
   share the Emacs =commandp= boundary.  Keep representative P2 key wiring and
   basic interactive dispatch resolved; follow-up P2/P6 work should focus on
   broader command dispatch and interactive behavior.

   budget at normalized form 4, =(require 'log-edit)=.  Per Doc 34,
   classify this as a Bootstrap/load (missing prerequisite replay)
   boundary, not a substrate defect.  When a vendor file wedges at a
   =require=, compute the full require closure and replay the
   prerequisites first, rather than treating the wedge as evidence of a
   missing substrate primitive.

   A 2026-07-03/04 follow-on progressed Doc 33 §4 item 11 (the 60-file
   upstream Org load-replay closure gate) to 44/60 files, reaching
   =sh-script.el=, where the child crashed executing the SMIE grammar
   computation at load time. Root-cause work traced this through four layers
   on the NeLisp side rather than the Org/vendor side: (1) NeLisp commit
   be928ab8 made native =defmacro= effective, un-deadening standalone-guarded
   code in this repo's bootstrap; (2) this repo's =src/emacs-keymap.el=
   had genuine circular aliases (=key-parse= and =key-valid-p= delegating
   back through their own unprefixed alias targets under the standalone
   guard) — FIXED 2026-07-04 in =src/emacs-keymap.el= by dispatching to
   the standalone implementations directly (host-Emacs behavior unchanged;
   the other 24 installs in =emacs-keymap-builtins.el= were audited and found
   non-circular); (3) unbounded lexframe recursion is now capped at depth 1000
   on the NeLisp side (branch =fix/native-defmacro-bootstrap-regression=,
   commit f55c12ef, a =max-lisp-eval-depth=-style unwind); (4) the
   remaining blocker is the documented NeLisp standalone GC root-coverage
   gap (vendor/nelisp =FINDINGS.md=): with the circular alias fixed,
   the regenerated bootstrap replays past the old crash region and now
   aborts later (exit 88) while defining a large nested-literal defun
   (=emacs-help-gui-writeback-spec=), and the full 60-file Org input segfaults
   at reader startup — both manifestations of the same GC root gap, which
   is being fixed on the NeLisp side (in-progress GC hot-path =let->let*=
   corrections).  Handoff: re-run the Org gate after the NeLisp GC root-gap
   work lands and the lexframe depth cap can be raised; do not debug the Org
   chain further until then.  The vendored checkout is pinned to f55c12ef
   plus the =format=/=make-temp-name= prelude patch (performance-load-bearing,
   still to be upstreamed).
211. Per-form interpreter cost (roughly 5-10s/form on heavy EIEIO/transient
   files) remains the throughput bound on these replays.  NeLisp runtime
   follow-ups — frame-push/arg-list allocation cost and runtime-image cold-load
   for the bootstrap+prelude prefix — are tracked on the NeLisp side, not here.
   2026-07-03 update: under NeLisp reader ed7a9789 (frame-push
   scratch-symbol sharing merged), the same 85-file =magit.el= chain that
   took about 788s earlier the same day now completes in about 621s (about
   21% faster) — record this as the current chain baseline.  The
   frame-push sharing change gave about 21% on this interpreter-heavy
   chain versus about 6% on light gates, so per-form interpreter cost
   remains the dominant throughput bound on EIEIO/transient-heavy replays.
   2026-07-03 feasibility finding: the =.nlri= runtime-image mechanism is
   text-source replay (it re-evaluates stored forms, so it has no startup win),
   and its compiled-artifact cache path is currently blocked at far smaller
   scale than the 2.5MB bootstrap (a 370KB source already timed out per NeLisp
   Doc 154).  The flat-arena cold-loader (=nl_cold_load_arena=) is a true heap
   snapshot/restore and would combine with =--repl= with zero harness changes,
   but the production single-chunk dump has a structural
   interned-region/relocation-table capacity wall (~106MB subset proven; the
   full bootstrap dump aborts per NeLisp Doc 156 §4).  Therefore no
   harness-only throughput shortcut exists; the path is NeLisp-side: integrate
   the multi-chunk streaming-dump (proven read-only in NeLisp boot-wiring
   12-14) into the production =nl_cold_load_arena=/=nl_cold_overwrite_globals=
   install path, then re-attempt a bootstrap-level dump.  Also note the
   cold-image =(setf (STRUCT-SLOT r) v)= abort risk (NeLisp Doc 156) is a
   validation prerequisite for EIEIO/transient-heavy vendor code before
   trusting cold-loaded gates.

   Both narrowed conjuncts were real and are fixed
   (=paragraph-indent-text-mode= via the backquote-free
   =define-derived-mode= bridge; =paragraph-indent-minor-mode= via the
   =emacs-easy-mmode--standalone-p= gate ordering fix); the
   =evaluated=nil= error among the first five conjuncts was the
   =(equal text-mode-hook ...)= conjunct -- the reader stdlib prelude's
   =equal= redefinition (Doc 22 A3) errors on EVERY call in the replay
   environment (reader-side, minimal repro in item 221).  An equal-free
   equivalent of the full strong proof now passes (=status=done=,
   40.27s).
220. Proof-mechanism bug found and fixed, 2026-07-04: every =status=done=
   recorded above via =make diagnose-vendor-repl-replay-fast=/
   =diagnose-vendor-repl-replay= (items 215, 216, 218, 219, and the §4
   item 11 Org claim) proved only that the vendor files loaded without a
   load-time error -- none of them actually proved their stated proof
   form.  Root cause, in =scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el='s
   =vendor-repl-standalone--write-input= (via the proof-scaffold-only use
   of the =vendor-repl-standalone--pretty-form= helper, which calls
   =pp-to-string=; the helper itself is unchanged and still used for the
   unrelated =VENDOR_REPL_COALESCE_FILE_FORMS= file-coalescing path): the
   proof scaffold emitted `(setq vendor-repl-proof-value (condition-case
   err <PROOF> (error ...)))` and the `(if vendor-repl-proof-value ...)`
   marker write as pretty-printed, MULTI-PHYSICAL-LINE forms.  This
   reader's =--repl= loop reads and evaluates exactly one physical line
   at a time with no continuation (NeLisp Doc 156 §7), so both forms were
   shredded into unrelated fragments: =vendor-repl-proof-value= stayed
   void, a fragment line consisting of just `(nl-write-file MARKER
   "VENDOR-REPL-STANDALONE=ok")` was a complete, valid, single-line form
   on its own and fired unconditionally, and the fail branch (referencing
   the never-bound =vendor-repl-proof-detail=) could never execute.  A
   second, independent problem: this reader's =condition-case=/
   =ignore-errors= discards the protected body's return value
   unconditionally, even on success (=(ignore-errors 42)= => nil), so
   even a single-line =condition-case= could not have captured the real
   proof value.

   Fix (=scripts/vendor-repl-standalone-replay.el=, this task's commit):
   every proof-scaffold form is now built as Lisp data and printed with
   =prin1-to-string= (single physical line, never =pp-to-string=), with
   =print-escape-newlines= bound so embedded string newlines cannot
   reintroduce a line break, plus a defensive newline strip.
   =condition-case= is no longer used to capture the proof value; instead
   =vendor-repl-proof-value= and a companion =vendor-repl-proof-evaluated=
   flag are both initialized to nil on their own line, then set together
   via a single-line `(setq vendor-repl-proof-value (prog1 <PROOF> (setq
   vendor-repl-proof-evaluated t)))` -- if the proof form itself errors,
   that whole physical line aborts before either side effect runs
   (tolerated by the REPL's per-line error handling), leaving both at
   their nil initializers, so an errored proof and a cleanly-false proof
   both correctly fail, and =evaluated= distinguishes the two for
   diagnosis.  =vendor-repl-standalone-proof-form-file= inputs with more
   than one top-level form now emit every form but the last as its own
   single-line side-effecting statement, capturing only the FINAL form's
   value as the proof (previously only the file's first form was even
   read, silently dropping the rest).  A new ERT test in
   =test/standalone-diagnostics-test.el= covers the multi-form case;
   the existing proof-scaffold test was updated to assert the new
   single-line shape instead of the old (buggy) =condition-case= shape.
   =make test-fast= shows the same 6 pre-existing failures as before this
   change (four =emacs-redisplay-test= failures plus
   =vendor-first-core-modes-test/lightweight-support-libraries-load-vendor-source='s
   =void-function Info-find-file=), no regressions.

   Sanity gates (=vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/ring.el=, single file,
   ~40s/run): a deliberately false proof =(and nil)= now correctly yields
   =status=fail=, =evaluated=t=; a deliberately true proof
   =(featurep 'ring)= now correctly yields =status=done=; a deliberately
   erroring proof (an undefined function call) yields =status=fail=,
   =evaluated=nil= -- confirming the mechanism distinguishes an errored
   proof from a cleanly-false one, and that a false/erroring proof no
   longer silently reports =done=.

   Honest re-run matrix with the fixed harness (see items 215/216/218/219
   above for full per-item detail and reconstruction caveats): the Org
   60/61-file chain's original 5-conjunct AND proof now FAILS
   (=featurep=/=fboundp org-element-parse-buffer= true, =fboundp=/
   =commandp org-mode= false); a reduced 3-conjunct Org proof passes.  The
   four non-Magit item 219 legs (outline/dired/dired-x/vc+vc-git)
   re-confirm =status=done=.  The =text-mode.el= strong proof now fails
   with a genuine evaluation error, narrowed to the
   =paragraph-indent-text-mode=/=paragraph-indent-minor-mode= conjuncts.
   Item 216's reconstructed magit-base proof fails cleanly, and a
   follow-up probe shows =magit-section-mode= never became fbound on that
   chain.  Item 218 (full 85-file Magit chain) was not re-run in this
   pass -- see its note above.  Emerging pattern across three independent
   files (org.el, text-mode.el, magit-section.el): a =define-derived-mode=
   whose PARENT is itself a mode symbol (=outline-mode=, =text-mode=,
   =special-mode=) does not reliably become fbound in this standalone
   reader, while the base case with a nil parent (plain
   =(define-derived-mode text-mode nil ...)=) does.  This pattern was not
   investigated further and no fix was attempted here, per this task's
   scope; it narrows, but does not resolve, the §4 item 11 org-mode gap.
   [Resolved same day at item 221: the true trigger is backquote-template
   macro bodies, not the parent argument; the parent-nil "success" cases
   were substrate defaliases, not surviving macro expansions.]

   Normalizer audit (this task's other ask): checked
   =scripts/standalone-source-normalize.el='s
   =standalone-source-normalize-large-defun-character-limit= (3500 chars)
   and its associated elision/dropped-symbol lists
   (=-elided-defun-symbols=, =-dropped-defun-symbols=, =-large-defun-p=,
   etc.) -- every one of them only ever matches on
   =(eq (car form) 'defun)=.  =define-derived-mode= forms have a
   different =car= entirely and are never inspected by =-large-defun-p=,
   so they are never truncated or elided by that mechanism; org.el's
   =(define-derived-mode org-mode outline-mode ...)= (measured 6247
   printed characters -- above the 3500 =defun= limit, but exempt from it
   because it is not a =defun=) passes through the normalizer's catch-all
   clause essentially unchanged, as a single ~6.2KB physical line.  There
   is also no dedicated =define-derived-mode= clause anywhere in
   =standalone-source-normalize-top-level-forms='s ~300-line dispatch
   cond.  So this task's leading hypothesis -- that the 3500-char defun
   truncation or an elision list drops org.el's =define-derived-mode=
   expansion -- is REFUTED by direct inspection; the normalizer does not
   touch it at all.  The real gap, per the pattern above, looks like a
   reader-side or macro-expansion-side issue specific to
   =define-derived-mode= calls with a non-nil parent, not a normalizer
   elision.  Do not implement an org-mode-specific normalizer workaround
   from this note alone -- the pattern needs confirming against the
   reader/macro-expansion path first, which is out of this task's scope.
221. The item 220 =define-derived-mode= pattern is ROOT-CAUSED and FIXED
   on the nelisp-emacs-lib side, 2026-07-04; §4 item 11's org-mode
   command gap is closed and §4 item 10's text-mode strong proof is
   resolved up to one reader-side residual.

   Root cause: NOT the parent argument, and NOT the normalizer (item 220
   had already ruled the latter out).  On the standalone bootstrap path,
   =define-derived-mode= is the Track H substrate bridge --
   =src/emacs-mode-builtins.el='s =defmacro= delegating to
   =src/emacs-mode.el='s =emacs-mode-define-derived-mode= -- and BOTH
   macro bodies were backquote templates.  In the standalone reader's
   replay environment, invoking a user-defined macro whose
   expansion-producing body is a backquote template signals an error on
   the invocation line, and the REPL's per-line error tolerance silently
   drops that one physical line: the entire single-line
   =(define-derived-mode CHILD PARENT ...)= normalized form vanishes with
   no visible failure.  Isolation (minimal repro files under the
   gitignored =tmp-diag/=): a plain list-built =defmacro= invoked from a
   replayed file works end-to-end (its expansion evaluated, result
   captured), while the semantically identical macro with a backquote
   body leaves its result =defvar= UNBOUND (the invocation line
   errored); =declare= clauses (=debug=/=doc-string=/=indent=, alone or
   combined exactly as vendor derived.el orders them), docstring size,
   and nesting depth are NOT factors.  Item 220's parent-nil vs
   non-nil asymmetry was an artifact: the "working" nil-parent cases
   (=text-mode= etc.) got their function cells from the substrate
   =defalias= bridges (=emacs-mode-text-mode= ...), not from a surviving
   macro expansion, while every child actually created through the macro
   (=org-mode=, =magit-section-mode=, =paragraph-indent-text-mode=) was
   lost.  The half-installed keymap-bound-but-function-void state matches
   exactly: =org-mode-map= etc. come from separate top-level =defvar= /
   =defvar-keymap= forms that replay fine; only the
   =define-derived-mode= call line was dropped.  (Cosmetic reader note
   for future probes: =macrop= reports nil for user-defined macros in
   this environment even when =fboundp= is t and invocation works.)

   Fix (this commit; vendor sources untouched; least-invasive substrate
   rewrite): =emacs-mode-define-derived-mode= (=src/emacs-mode.el=) and
   the =define-derived-mode= bridge (=src/emacs-mode-builtins.el=)
   rewritten with explicit =list=/=append=/=quote= construction --
   expansion unchanged, host ERT =emacs-mode-builtins-test= 18/18.
   Three companion substrate fixes found while closing the §4 item 10
   text-mode strong-proof residue, same commit: (i)
   =emacs-easy-mmode--standalone-p= (=src/emacs-easy-mmode.el=) gains a
   =(not (fboundp 'define-minor-mode))= arm -- the bootstrap loads
   =emacs-stub-bulk= LAST (Doc 22 A19), so the old
   =(get 'define-minor-mode 'emacs-stub-bulk)= test could never be true
   at easy-mmode load time, the fallback never installed, and stub-bulk's
   no-op =define-minor-mode= macro silently defined nothing (now
   =paragraph-indent-minor-mode= is a real command); (ii)
   =src/emacs-stub-bulk.el= gains a =syntax-table-p= stub recognizing all
   three substrate syntax-table shapes (the =emacs-syntax-table.el=
   char-table subtype, =emacs-stub.el='s =(syntax-table . PARENT)= cons
   -- the shape actually live in the replay bootstrap -- and the
   256-slot vector fallback); (iii) =src/emacs-mode-builtins.el= no
   longer pre-defvars =text-mode-hook= to nil, so vendor text-mode.el's
   replayed default =\'(text-mode-hook-identify)= takes effect.

   Reader-side residuals recorded, NOT fixed here (out of scope; fixes
   belong in dev/nelisp):
   - The reader stdlib prelude
     (=vendor/nelisp/scripts/nelisp-stdlib-prelude.el=, its Doc 22 A3
     =equal= redefinition) makes EVERY subsequent =(equal ...)= call
     error.  Minimal repro: bare reader, =(load
     ".../nelisp-stdlib-prelude.el")=, then =(equal 1 1)= errors (the
     line is dropped); without the prelude the same call returns t.
     This blocks the ORIGINAL item 10 strong-proof file's single
     =(equal text-mode-hook ...)= conjunct; the equal-free equivalent
     passes (matrix below).
   - The backquote-macro-invocation failure itself is reader-side.  The
     substrate fix removes backquote from the bootstrap-path macros, but
     any vendor chain that replays =emacs-lisp/derived.el= will
     re-shadow =define-derived-mode= with the vendor backquote-template
     macro and re-break (observed directly: after derived.el replays,
     =define-derived-mode= is fbound but broken, and even a nil-parent
     child never becomes fbound).  None of the verified chains below
     include derived.el.  The durable resolution is fixing backquote
     macro invocation in the reader.
   - =make-syntax-table= in the replay bootstrap resolves to
     =emacs-stub.el='s cons fallback even though
     =emacs-syntax-table.el='s char-table version appears later with an
     install gate that should fire; un-investigated residual.

   Verification matrix (fixed, sanity-gated harness; normalized cache
   warm; one reader at a time; final bootstrap with all four substrate
   fixes):
   - (a) minimal repro chain (repro file only), proof =(and (fboundp
     'repro-mode-a) (fboundp 'repro-mode-b) (commandp 'repro-mode-a)
     (commandp 'repro-mode-b))= (nil-parent + non-nil-parent children):
     =status=done= 40.27s (pre-fix: all four conjuncts nil).
   - (b) magit-base 7-file chain (compat/cond-let/llama/transient/

     fbound on this chain).
   - (c) text-mode.el strong proof: the equal-free equivalent (12
     conjuncts, including the =text-mode-hook= value shape,
     =syntax-table-p=, and BOTH =commandp paragraph-indent-text-mode=
     and =commandp paragraph-indent-minor-mode=): =status=done= 40.27s.
     The original file remains blocked ONLY by the reader-side =equal=
     defect above.
   - (d) THE Org gate: the exact 61-file chain from item 215's honest
     re-run (recovered verbatim from that run's session log) with the
     ORIGINAL 5-conjunct proof =(and (featurep 'org) (featurep
     'org-element) (fboundp 'org-mode) (fboundp
     'org-element-parse-buffer) (commandp 'org-mode))=: =status=done=,
     exit=0, 249.76s (pre-fix honest run: =status=fail= 251.03s with
     =fboundp=/=commandp org-mode= false).  §4 item 11 is now genuinely
     DONE.

     still =status=fail=, =evaluated=t= (cleanly false), 102.16s -- the
     mode-install blocker is gone per (b), so item 216's remaining gap
     is in its section/overlay/marker/display legs, not in mode
     installation; it stays OPEN there.

     =emacs-redisplay-test= + =Info-find-file=), no new failures.  Host
     ERT =emacs-mode-builtins-test=: 18/18.

222. Buffer/major-mode substrate gap: inside =with-temp-buffer=,
   =major-mode= evaluated to nil (even with no mode call, and even
   after an explicit =(fundamental-mode)= call inside the temp
   buffer), and =(with-temp-buffer (org-mode) t)= silently returned
   nil instead of t -- no crash, no visible error.  ROOT-CAUSED and
   FIXED, 2026-07-04.

   Root cause: NOT specific to =major-mode= at all.  Minimal probes
   against the persistent bootstrap REPL (single-line forms per the
   item 220/221 fixed proof-scaffold harness) showed that EVERY
   =with-temp-buffer= body -- =major-mode=, =(boundp 'major-mode)=,
   =(buffer-name)=, a plain literal =t= -- came back nil:
   =(with-temp-buffer major-mode)= nil,
   =(with-temp-buffer (boundp 'major-mode))= => nil,
   =(with-temp-buffer (buffer-name))= => nil,
   while top-level =major-mode= was the expected =fundamental-mode=
   and =(boundp 'major-mode)= was t.  That pattern (every
   =with-temp-buffer= body value replaced by nil, regardless of what
   the body actually computes) means =with-temp-buffer= itself never
   propagates its body's value on this reader -- =major-mode= being
   nil was just the specific symptom that exposed a generic bug.
   =src/emacs-buffer-builtins.el='s =with-temp-buffer= macro is
   already backquote-free (list/cons construction) and expands to
   =(let ((buf (nelisp-ec-generate-new-buffer " *temp*")))
   (unwind-protect (nelisp-ec-with-current-buffer buf BODY...)
   (nelisp-ec-kill-buffer buf)))=; the actual defect is one layer
   down, in =nelisp-ec-with-current-buffer= itself
   (=src/nelisp-emacs-compat.el=), which was written as a BACKQUOTE
   TEMPLATE.  This is the exact same standalone-reader defect item
   221 root-caused for =define-derived-mode= (invoking a
   user-defined macro whose expansion-producing body is a backquote
   template misbehaves on this reader) -- but item 221 only observed
   the "top-level invocation line is silently dropped" symptom
   (macro called for side effect at file-replay top level).  Here the
   backquote-bodied macro is invoked from *inside* another
   expression's runtime evaluation (nested inside =unwind-protect=,
   inside =let=), and the failure mode is different: instead of the
   whole line being dropped, the nested call silently evaluates to
   nil instead of BODY's value.  =src/emacs-buffer-builtins.el='s own
   =buffer-hash= function already carried a comment noting this
   symptom ("the return value of =with-current-buffer=/
   =save-restriction=... this runtime does not propagate") but had
   worked around it with an explicit =setq= capture instead of
   diagnosing the backquote-invocation root cause.  Three sibling
   macros in the same file share the identical defect:
   =nelisp-ec-save-excursion=, =nelisp-ec-save-restriction=,
   =nelisp-ec-save-current-buffer= -- all backquote templates, all
   silently discarding their body's value on this reader, which
   backs the unprefixed =save-excursion=/=save-restriction=/
   =save-current-buffer= bridges in =emacs-buffer-builtins.el= used
   throughout the substrate and by nearly every vendor Elisp file.

   Fix (=src/nelisp-emacs-compat.el=; vendor sources untouched):
   =nelisp-ec-with-current-buffer=, =nelisp-ec-save-excursion=,
   =nelisp-ec-save-restriction=, and =nelisp-ec-save-current-buffer=
   rewritten with explicit =list=/=cons=/=append= construction
   (same style as item 221's =define-derived-mode= fix) --
   expansion unchanged, body-value propagation now correct.  New
   host ERT suite =test/nelisp-emacs-compat-test.el= (this module had
   no dedicated test file before this fix despite backing T39's ~37
   =nelisp-ec-*= APIs): 13/13 passing, covering body-value
   propagation and restore-on-normal-exit/restore-on-error for all
   four macros.  Under host Emacs these tests cannot reproduce the
   standalone-only failure (host backquote works fine), so they pin
   the functional contract rather than the reader defect; the
   standalone reproduction lives in the verification matrix below.

   Verification matrix:
   - (a) minimal probes, persistent bootstrap only (no vendor files),
     single-line forms, before vs. after the fix:
     =(with-temp-buffer major-mode)= nil -> =fundamental-mode=;
     =(with-temp-buffer (boundp 'major-mode))= nil -> t;
     =(with-temp-buffer (buffer-name))= nil -> =" *temp*<3>"=;
     =(with-temp-buffer (fundamental-mode) major-mode)= nil ->
     =fundamental-mode=; =(with-temp-buffer t)= nil -> t.  Also
     confirmed (pre-existing, documented, NOT part of this fix):
     =major-mode= has no real per-buffer isolation in this substrate
     yet (Track H's own commentary: "simulating buffer-local via the
     convention that they're re-set every time" -- =emacs-mode.el=
     keeps =major-mode= as a plain global defvar with no buffer-local
     store), so a =setq= of =major-mode= inside =with-temp-buffer=
     is still visible after the temp buffer is killed; this is an
     orthogonal, already-known gap, not touched here.
   - (b) the real upstream Org chain: the item 215/221 61-file file
     list was not preserved (same caveat as item 215/216), so this
     verification reconstructed an equivalent chain by computing
     host Emacs's =(require 'org)(require 'org-element)= closure
     restricted to =vendor/emacs-lisp/= (and subdirectories) on
     =load-path=, filtered to drop any file whose feature is already
     satisfied by the persistent bootstrap (137 features queried
     live from the bootstrap REPL).  Two corrections were needed
     beyond that filter, both recorded here for future re-runs: (i)
     =org.el='s top-level =(eval-when-compile (require 'gnus-sum))=
     behaves as =progn= under a plain host =load= of an uncompiled
     file and pulls in the entire gnus/message/mail/epa web (~90
     extra files) -- =scripts/standalone-source-normalize.el= already
     drops top-level =eval-when-compile= entirely for exactly this
     reason, so a fake =(provide 'gnus-sum)= before requiring org
     correctly matches the normalized replay; (ii) the naive host
     closure also autoload-pulls real =vendor/emacs-lisp/emacs-lisp/
     derived.el= the moment any file's top-level
     =(define-derived-mode ...)= call is reached (because a bare
     host Emacs session, unlike the persistent bootstrap, has no
     =define-derived-mode= defined yet and falls back to Emacs's own
     =derived= autoload) -- this file must NOT be part of the replay
     chain: item 221 already documented that replaying real
     =derived.el= re-shadows the substrate's fixed
     =define-derived-mode= with the broken backquote-template vendor
     version and re-breaks every mode defined afterward, and none of
     item 221's verified chains included it.  After both corrections
     the reconstructed chain is 68 files (recorded at
     =tmp-diag/org-chain-68-files-item222.txt=, gitignored scratch,
     for reuse -- preserving it this time since the 60/61-file list
     from item 215 was lost).  Loads clean, =status=done=,
     =load-ok-count=68/68=.  A proof restricted to conjuncts safe to
     evaluate (see next paragraph for why) --
     =(and (featurep 'org) (featurep 'org-element) (fboundp
     'org-mode) (fboundp 'org-element-parse-buffer) (commandp
     'org-mode) (with-temp-buffer (fundamental-mode) (eq major-mode
     'fundamental-mode)) (with-temp-buffer t))= -- =status=done=,
     exit=0, elapsed 459.76s.  This confirms item 221's org-mode
     fboundp/commandp result still holds on the corrected chain, and
     confirms this item's with-temp-buffer body-value fix holds with
     the full real Org dependency graph loaded, not just against the
     bare persistent bootstrap.
   - (b'), NOT part of this fix, new gap found and NOT chased per
     task scope: the literal verification-(b) proof requested,
     =(with-temp-buffer (org-mode) (eq major-mode 'org-mode))=,
     could not be completed -- actually INVOKING =(org-mode)= (its
     real function body, not just =fboundp=/=commandp= introspection)
     hangs on this reader.  Isolated with a plain top-level
     =(progn (org-mode) (eq major-mode 'org-mode))= (no
     =with-temp-buffer= involved at all) on the corrected 68-file
     chain: =status=fail=, =timed-out=t=, =exit=124= at the 560s
     internal timeout, sentinel stuck at =proof:start= (the call
     never returns).  This is a DIFFERENT gap from item 221's (which
     was about =org-mode= never becoming fbound at all): here
     =org-mode= is genuinely fboundp/commandp per (b) above, but
     running its real body -- customization/keymap/abbrev/regexp
     setup done by the =define-derived-mode= body plus
     =org-set-regexps-and-options= and friends -- does not complete
     in reasonable time.  (A first attempt at this same check
     appeared to fail fast via an apparent crash, but that run was
     contaminated by a leftover concurrent =vendor/nelisp/target/
     nelisp= reader process from an unrelated, unfinished
     session sharing this checkout -- consistent with the
     shared-checkout hazard noted at the top of this task; that
     process was killed and the check re-run cleanly, which is what
     produced the 560s hang result above.)  Root cause unexplored;
     out of scope for this item (buffer/major-mode substrate, not
     org-mode body semantics) and not chased per instructions.  (c)
     (=org-element-parse-buffer= smoke) was not attempted given (b')
     since it also starts by calling =(org-mode)=.
   - =make test-fast=: the same 6 known failures (four
     =emacs-redisplay-test= + =Info-find-file=), no new failures.
     Host ERT =nelisp-emacs-compat-test= (new suite for this
     item): 13/13.

   Files touched: =src/nelisp-emacs-compat.el= (fix, four macros),
   =test/nelisp-emacs-compat-test.el= (new host ERT suite).

223. Item 222(b') follow-up: actually INVOKING =(org-mode)='s real body is
   ROOT-CAUSED as a dev/nelisp reader/runtime defect (GC root-coverage
   gap), 2026-07-04.  STOPPED per task scope -- this is a reader
   primitive defect, not a nelisp-emacs-lib substrate gap; no fix
   applied here, no substrate files touched.

   [2026-07-04 correction (item 225): the behavior probed in this item
   was measured against replay chains that contained the hollow
   =(defmacro backquote (form))= emission later diagnosed in dev/nelisp
   merge =69301d56= and root-caused/fixed as item 225 -- every
   backquote-built macro loaded after that point in the chain
   (=org-with-wide-buffer=, =org-no-read-only=, ...) silently expanded
   to nil, so large parts of =org-mode='s real initialization were
   silently SKIPPED, not executed.  This item's GC observations
   (=nl_kw_is_keyword= SIGSEGV signature, cold-boot vs. replay-load
   manifestations) were made on that partially-skipped workload and
   remain factual for it, but the workload itself was not the honest
   full =org-mode= init.  Per dev/nelisp =FINDINGS.md= (2026-07-04,
   post-workaround): with backquote genuinely working, real full
   =(org-mode)= init is a superlinear-cost computation on the current
   interpreter (no macroexpansion cache + per-bind deep clone;
   >20 s / ~900 MB RSS within 5 s for =(with-temp-buffer (org-mode) t)=)
   -- interpreter performance work (macroexpansion cache, bind-path
   allocation fast path) is the true remaining blocker, and it is
   pending in dev/nelisp.]

   Environment: dev/nelisp =main= @ =a679a31a= (canonical checkout,
   read/run-only for this task; a local comment-only working-tree diff
   to =scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el= was present at investigation
   time from unrelated concurrent work sharing that checkout -- verified
   by inspection to touch only prose comments, not code, in the
   =nl_gc_in_arena=/=nl_gc_mark_published_contexts_from= region; dev/nelisp
   =main= has since advanced further, to =0e599c29=, via that same
   concurrent activity -- this item's reproduction is pinned to the
   =a679a31a=-era binary, sha1 =6581d44a8f95caf7f080c0e05f75cf2aa144d5ff=,
   built before HEAD moved further).  =nelisp-emacs-lib='s own
   =build/nemacs-bootstrap.{el,repl}= (gitignored artifacts) were
   regenerated via =make build-nelisp-bootstrap= from this branch's
   =28f728d= (item 222's fix) before use, per task instructions; this
   is a generated-artifact refresh only, no tracked file changed.
   Reproduction used dev/nelisp's =scripts/cold-image-org-e2e.sh 1= (its
   own default, faster prelude -- =NELISP_E2E_KEEP=1=) against the
   checked-in 60-file Org chain (=scripts/cold-image-org-e2e-files.txt=)
   with the refreshed bootstrap-repl: host .repl generation 908ms,
   replay-load 9.98s, dump 0.76s, cold boot 0.87s; faithfulness probe
   =(featurep 'org) (featurep 'org-element) (fboundp 'org-mode) (fboundp
   'org-element-parse-buffer) (commandp 'org-mode) (fboundp 'commandp)=
   = =(t t t t (interactive) t)=, identical replay vs. cold-boot -- so
   this reproduction independently reconfirms item 221/222's org-mode
   fboundp/commandp result before hitting the new gap below.

   Reproduction, two distinct manifestations of (evidently) the same
   defect depending on process state:
   - Cold-booted process (=--cold-load-from IMG=, image already
     ~693 MB): =(with-temp-buffer (org-mode) t)=, and the bare top-level
     =(progn (org-mode) (eq major-mode 'org-mode))= with no
     =with-temp-buffer= at all, both SIGSEGV deterministically (3/3
     repeats; =ulimit -s unlimited= makes no difference, ruling out a
     stack-depth/guard-page explanation) in ~1.5s wall (barely past
     cold-boot-to-first-eval time) -- this is a CRASH, not a hang.
   - The SAME probe against a freshly replay-loaded (non-cold) process
     (append the probe to the e2e script's own =load-only.repl= tail and
     run through =./target/nelisp --repl=) does NOT crash within 60s --
     it HANGS (=timeout 60= => exit 124, no output) -- consistent with
     (and reproducing) item 222(b')'s originally reported 560s-timeout
     hang with the sentinel stuck at =proof:start=.  The two process
     shapes (cold-booted vs. replay-loaded) manifest differently
     (immediate null-deref crash vs. non-terminating loop) from what
     bisection below shows is the same underlying corruption; plausibly
     the freed/blanked bytes a collection leaves behind happen to be
     all-zero in the cold-boot arena layout (an immediate null deref)
     but form an unintended self-referential (non-terminating) chain in
     the replay-process's arena layout instead of a null.

   Bisection (single-line probes, one session, same cold image):
   - Parents run clean and fast: =(with-temp-buffer (fundamental-mode)
     t)=, =(with-temp-buffer (text-mode) t)=, =(with-temp-buffer
     (outline-mode) t)= all => =t=, exit 0, sub-second.  So the defect is
     specific to =org-mode='s OWN =define-derived-mode= body (the
     customization/keymap/abbrev/regexp/font-lock setup done by
     =org-set-regexps-and-options= and friends per item 222's note), not
     to the derived-mode parent-call chain, and not to =with-temp-buffer=
     (the bare top-level call crashes identically).
   - GDB (=gdb --batch -ex run -ex bt=) on the crashing cold-boot probe:
     SIGSEGV at =nl_kw_is_keyword+136=, instruction =movzbq
     (%rdi),%rax= with =%rdi=0=.  Backtrace (top): =nl_kw_is_keyword= <-
     =nl_eval_inner= <- =nelisp_eval_call= <- =nl_sf_progn_body_step= <-
     =nl_sf_progn_get_cdr= <- =nl_sf_progn_step= <- =nl_sf_progn_eval_step=
     <- =nl_sf_progn_body_step= <- ... (repeats) <- =nl_sf_progn= <-
     =nl_apply_special= <- ... <- =nl_sf_let_*= <- ... <- =nl_driver_eval_published=.
     =nl_kw_is_keyword= (the M4 keyword-self-eval fast path wired into
     =nl_eval_inner=, scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el lines
     13467-13480) checks, in order, =(sexp-tag form) = 4= (Symbol) then
     =(str-len form) > 0= then =(str-byte-at form 0)= -- both of the
     first two checks must have PASSED to reach the crashing
     instruction (disassembly confirms =%rip= is past both branches, at
     the =str-byte-at= read), meaning =form= itself is a live,
     correctly-tagged Symbol with a recorded non-zero name length, but
     the SEPARATELY-ALLOCATED name-buffer this length refers to has a
     null data pointer.  I.e. the Symbol's container survived, but its
     name buffer did not -- freed/blanked while still referenced, mid
     nested-=progn=-body evaluation.
   - This crash signature (=nl_kw_is_keyword(NULL)=) is IDENTICAL to a
     pre-existing, already-documented, not-fully-resolved defect
     recorded directly in dev/nelisp's own build script
     (scripts/nelisp-standalone-build.el lines 12949-12961): "the
     anvil-pkg suite trips a root-coverage gap ... a collection frees a
     still-referenced cons, blanking a progn body form ->
     nl_kw_is_keyword(NULL)".  That comment records the fix attempted
     for THAT workload (mark+sweep GC + conservative native-stack scan,
     both currently active per lines 12926/12962) and explicitly notes
     the alternative GC mode (compaction) has an analogous unresolved
     gap, just a different manifestation ("move+munmap dangling vs
     free+reuse blanking").  =(org-mode)='s real body -- deep nested
     =progn=/=let=, heavy consing for regexp/keyword-table/face-alist
     construction inside =org-set-regexps-and-options= and friends --
     re-triggers the SAME root-coverage class, in a shape the existing
     mitigation does not cover.  (Doc 149's string/symbol name-buffer
     clone-ALIASING optimization, flag =268435648=1=, sharing a name
     buffer across clones instead of deep-copying, is also a plausible
     contributing/compounding factor for why a Symbol's name buffer
     specifically goes missing, but this was not isolated further.)
   - Attempted a minimal repro independent of Org: a FLAT 80-form
     top-level =(let ((x 1)) (progn (setq big0 (make-vector 200000 0))
     ... (eq x x)))= (~128 MB of allocation, comfortably past the 16 MiB
     GC trigger) on the plain bootstrap REPL (no vendor files) ran clean,
     =t=, no crash.  So raw allocation volume through a SHALLOW =progn=
     is NOT sufficient; the defect needs the deep nested
     =progn=/=let=/function-call shape actually produced by
     =define-derived-mode='s expansion of =org-mode='s body (matching the
     multi-frame =nl_sf_progn_*= recursion seen in the backtrace). A
     smaller synthetic repro reproducing the nesting shape was not found
     within this task's time budget; the checked-in 60-file Org chain
     (=scripts/cold-image-org-e2e-files.txt=) plus either probe above
     remains the smallest known repro.
   - Not chased further per task instructions (this is a dev/nelisp
     reader/GC defect, out of scope to fix from nelisp-emacs-lib, and
     dev/nelisp is read/run-only for this task): the exact mark-phase
     root-coverage hole (which live root the conservative native-stack
     scan or GC mark walk fails to find for this call shape) was not
     isolated inside dev/nelisp's C-shaped Elisp-DSL GC implementation.

   Verification (honest, not achieved): item 222(b')'s requested
   =(with-temp-buffer (org-mode) (eq major-mode 'org-mode))= still does
   NOT complete -- SIGSEGV on cold boot, hangs (timeout) on replay-load,
   both reproduced above.  =org-element-parse-buffer= smoke was not
   attempted (unchanged from item 222, still gated on this).  No
   nelisp-emacs-lib substrate files were touched, so =make test-fast= was
   not re-run for this item; the item 221/222 fixes on this branch
   (=28f728d=) are unaffected.

   Disposition: STOP, per task instructions -- this is a reader-side
   (dev/nelisp) primitive/GC defect, not a substrate gap.  The fix
   belongs in dev/nelisp's garbage collector (root-coverage for a
   Symbol's name-buffer pointer, and/or the progn-body "remaining
   forms" cons, when reachable only through deep native call frames
   during heavy nested-progn/let evaluation) -- out of scope for this
   repository and not attempted here.

   design-doc entry and the gitignored =build/nemacs-bootstrap.{el,repl}=
   artifacts, regenerated from already-committed =28f728d= sources, no
   tracked change).

224. Item 223 practical workaround VERIFIED and SHIPPED as this
   substrate's default =org-modules=, 2026-07-04.  Between item 223 and
   this item, dev/nelisp =main= landed the STACK_TOP-after-cold-load-grow
   GC fix (=1cfb42f4=/=cf5a8067=) and root-caused the remaining
   =(org-mode)= hang to genuinely loading the real vendored Gnus package
   via =(require 'ol-gnus)= (dev/nelisp =FINDINGS.md=, "root-cause
   (org-mode) practical hang to require'ing real Gnus", 2026-07-04) --
   this item verifies the practical, non-reader-touching workaround that
   FINDINGS.md's remediation proposal item 3 flagged but did not apply,
   and ships it as this repository's shipped default.

   [2026-07-04 correction (item 225): this item's headline timings --
   =(with-temp-buffer (org-mode) (eq major-mode 'org-mode))= completing
   in 0.8-5 s over the shipped 10-module default -- were measured
   against cold images whose replay chains contained the hollow
   =(defmacro backquote (form))= emission diagnosed in dev/nelisp merge
   =69301d56= and fixed as item 225.  With backquote hollowed, every
   backquote-built macro body after that point silently expanded to nil,
   so those runs paid for only PART of =org-mode='s real initialization;
   the "fast activation" partially reflected silently-skipped init, not
   honest full init.  The =org-modules= default shipped by this item
   remains valid and shipped (it removes a real, independently
   root-caused Gnus-loading cost), and the =(void-function \`)= gap this
   item recorded for =org-element-parse-buffer= was a downstream symptom
   of the same hollow-backquote clobber.  The honest revised picture per
   dev/nelisp =FINDINGS.md= (2026-07-04, post-workaround): with backquote
   genuinely working, real full =(org-mode)= init does NOT complete in
   practical time on the current interpreter (superlinear cost from
   re-expanding macros at every call plus per-bind deep cloning) --
   interpreter performance work in dev/nelisp (macroexpansion cache,
   bind-path fast path) is pending and is the true gate for honest
   =org-mode= activation timings.]

   Environment note: dev/nelisp's =./target/nelisp= on disk at task start
   (mtime 18:07) predated the STACK_TOP fix commit (=cf5a8067=, committed
   19:20) by about an hour -- rebuilt via =make standalone-reader= before
   any probing (dev/nelisp =main= @ =e25b244f=, read/run-only, no commits

   embedded in the generated bundle (see below).  All probes used
   dev/nelisp's =scripts/cold-image-org-e2e.sh 1= (=NELISP_E2E_KEEP=1=)
   against the checked-in 60-file Org chain
   (=scripts/cold-image-org-e2e-files.txt=); faithfulness conjuncts
   =(featurep 'org) (featurep 'org-element) (fboundp 'org-mode) (fboundp

   =(t t t t (interactive) t)=, identical replay-loaded vs. cold-booted,

   Probe 1, per task step 1: =(setq org-modules nil)= then
   =(with-temp-buffer (org-mode) (eq major-mode 'org-mode))=, single
   process, cold-booted image, no =timeout= wrapper needed (=timeout 120=

   fix is in place -- no further bisection needed.

   Probe 2, per task step 2: incremental =org-modules= growth, one fresh
   cold-booted process per length (=timeout 60= per addition), each
   running the real =(with-temp-buffer (org-mode) (eq major-mode
   'org-mode))=, over upstream =org.el='s literal 11-member default
   (=vendor/emacs-lisp/org/org.el:746=) with =ol-gnus= excluded and the
   other 10 added in their original list order:

   | list length | module added | wall time | result |
   |-------------+--------------+-----------+--------|
   |           1 | =ol-doi=     |    0.828s |    =t= |
   |           2 | =ol-w3m=     |    0.830s |    =t= |
   |           3 | =ol-bbdb=    |    1.235s |    =t= |
   |           4 | =ol-bibtex=  |    1.901s |    =t= |
   |           5 | =ol-docview= |    2.623s |    =t= |
   |           6 | =ol-info=    |    2.641s |    =t= |
   |           7 | =ol-irc=     |    2.639s |    =t= (*) |
   |           8 | =ol-mhe=     |    2.647s |    =t= |
   |           9 | =ol-rmail=   |    3.133s |    =t= |
   |          10 | =ol-eww=     |    4.840s |    =t= |

   (*) At list length 7 the bare 2-line probe (=setq= then the
   =with-temp-buffer= form as the last and only other line) printed a
   *blank* line instead of =t=, reproducible 5/5 identical reruns.
   Wrapping the identical expression in =(format "RESULT=<%S>" ...)=, or
   simply following it with any further top-level form (e.g. =(+ 1 1)=),
   both print =t=/=<t>= correctly every time; =(condition-case e ... (error
   ...))= around it never triggers the =error= handler either.  This is a
   REPL/print-vs-process-exit race specific to being the last thing
   evaluated before stdin =EOF= (not reproduced at any other list length in
   this same sweep), not a real semantic defect in =org-mode= at this
   =org-modules= length -- noted honestly per task instructions but not
   chased (out of scope; a dev/nelisp REPL-harness quirk, not this
   repository's substrate).  All 10 non-=ol-gnus= default members load and
   let =(org-mode)= complete within single-digit seconds; none needed
   further exclusion.  The full standard default *minus only =ol-gnus=* is
   therefore the "largest practical default" the task asked for -- no
   narrower list is needed.

   Fix (=src/emacs-init.el=; vendor =org.el= untouched): added, directly
   after the existing vendor =org/gnus= =load-path= wiring block (the
   thematically matching spot -- this is where =org=/=gnus= vendor
   subdirectories already get added to =load-path=),

   #+begin_src elisp
   (unless (boundp 'org-modules)
     (setq org-modules '(ol-doi ol-w3m ol-bbdb ol-bibtex ol-docview
                          ol-info ol-irc ol-mhe ol-rmail ol-eww)))
   #+end_src

   This relies on standard Elisp =defcustom=/=custom-declare-variable=
   semantics: a =defcustom= only installs its own default when the
   variable is not yet =default-boundp=, so pre-binding =org-modules= here,
   before any (present or future) load of real vendor =org.el=, makes
   upstream's own =(defcustom org-modules '(ol-doi ... ol-gnus ...) ...)=
   a no-op for the value (its docstring/=:type=/etc. metadata still
   installs normally) -- vendor =org.el= is never edited.  Verified this
   interpreter implements that same "don't clobber if already bound"
   semantics (not a given for a from-scratch DSL) with an isolated probe
   independent of Org: =(setq my-test-var '(foo)) (defcustom my-test-var
   '(bar baz) "doc string") my-test-var= on the plain persistent bootstrap
   (no vendor files) prints =(foo)=, =my-test-var=, =(foo)= -- i.e. the
   =defcustom= form itself evaluates (returning the symbol, like
   =defvar=), but the pre-existing value survives untouched, exactly
   matching real Emacs behavior and confirming the override mechanism is
   sound on this reader. This changes only this substrate's *default*; it
   does not disable =ol-gnus= for a real end user with Gnus actually
   configured, and it matches what a real user without Gnus would already
   experience (a fast =file-missing= skip via
   =org-load-modules-maybe='s own =condition-case-unless-debug=).
   =ol-gnus= (or any other module later found impractical) can be restored
   once the interpreter gains a macroexpansion cache or a bind-path
   allocation fast path (dev/nelisp =FINDINGS.md='s remediation proposal
   items 1-2).

   Verification matrix (honest, per task step 4):
   - Regenerated =build/nemacs-bootstrap.{el,repl}= via =make
     build-nelisp-bootstrap= (=files=124=); confirmed by =grep= that the

     replays, not just a source-tree change.

   - Cold-booted this new image and, with *no manual =setq= in the probe
     at all* (relying purely on the shipped default): =org-modules= =>
     =(ol-doi ol-w3m ol-bbdb ol-bibtex ol-docview ol-info ol-irc ol-mhe

     (org-mode) (eq major-mode 'org-mode))= => =t=; =status=0=, total
